Methylene Blue (MB), a cationic dye, initially forms a stable inclusion complex with beta-CD, which can be detected electrochemically or spectroscopically due to MB's distinct properties. When Quinine, an alkaloid with a higher binding affinity for beta-CD than MB, is introduced into the system, it competes for the same binding site within the beta-CD cavity. Because Quinine's molecular structure and hydrophobicity allow it to fit more snugly and interact more strongly with beta-CD, it effectively displaces MB from the complex. This displacement releases free MB into the solution, leading to a measurable change in the electrochemical or optical signal. The magnitude of this signal change correlates with the concentration of Quinine, enabling its sensitive detection. The process relies on the differential binding affinities of MB and Quinine for beta-CD, and the sensor's selectivity and sensitivity are governed by these host-guest interactions.", 'key_concepts':
